.I 95
.L 4
.F Reatha Holt <rholt6@jhu.edu>
.S Student Defense: Kunal Lillaney,  Johns Hopkins University - April 4 ,2019-11:00 AM Malone 228
.D Thu, 4 Apr 2019 13:21:42 +0000
.M
Ph.D. Candidate: Kunal Lillaney

Date & Time: Thursday,  April 4, 2019 at 11:00 AM- 1:00 PM

Location: Malone 228

Title: Building Hierarchical Storage Services in the Cloud

Abstract:
Object storage has emerged as a low-cost and scalable alternative solution in the cloud for storing unstructured data. However, performance limitations often compel users to employ supplementary storage services for their varied workloads. The result is growing storage sprawl, unacceptably low performance, and an increase in associated storage costs. We combine the assets of multiple cloud service on offer to develop NDStore, a scalable multi-hierarchical data storage deployment for open-science data in the cloud. It utilizes object storage as scalable base tier and an in-memory cluster as a low-latency caching tier to support a variety of workloads.
Moreover, many applications that are reliant on richer file system APIs and semantics are unable to benefit from object storage. Users either transfer data between a file system and object storage or use inefficient file connectors over object stores. One promising solution to this problem is providing dual access, the ability to transparently read and write the same data through both, file system interfaces and object storage APIs. We discuss features which we believe are essential or desirable in a dual-access object storage file system-OSFS. Further, we design and implement Agni, an efficient dual-access OSFS, utilizing only standard object storage APIs and capabilities. Generic object storage's lack of support for partial writes introduces a performance penalty for some workloads. Agni overcomes this shortcomings by implementing a multi-tier data structure which temporally indexes partial writes from the file system, persists them to a log, and merges them asynchronously for eventually consistent access through the object interface. Our experiments demonstrate that Agni improves partial write performance by two to seven times with minimal indexing overhead and for some representative workloads it can improve performance by 20%- 60% compared to S3FS, a popular OSFS, or the prevalent approach of manually copying data between different storage systems.

Website:
http://cs.jhu.edu/~klillan1/ <http://cs.jhu.edu/~klillan1/>

Biography:
Kunal Lillaney is a Ph.D. candidate in the Department of Computer Science at Johns Hopkins University, working with Randal Burns in the Hopkins Storage Systems Lab (HSSL). His research focuses on enabling big data in the cloud by building hierarchical storage services over object storage. He received his B.Engg degree in Computer Engineering from University of Mumbai in 2011 and his MSE degree in Computer Science from Johns Hopkins University in 2013. During his Ph.D., Kunal has interned with IBM Research-Almaden and Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory. He has also served as the Secretary of the Upsilon Pi Epsilon (UPE)-JHU Chapter between 2015 and 2017, and won the UPE Executive Council Award in 2016.


Reatha Holt
Sr. Administrative Coordinator
Johns Hopkins University
Computer Science Department
Malone 160
410-516-8775

Summary: The Grammy award-winning Silkroad Ensemble seeks and practices radical cultural collaboration in many forms, including creating and presenting new music.

Express your stress workshop (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/05/express-your-stress-workshop-0/)
When: Friday, 5-7pm
Where: Ames Hall, Homewood Campus
Summary: Express Your Stress is a free workshop created to give Hopkins students a fun opportunity to relieve stress and learn how to use art to improve their well-being. Peggy Kolodny, a professional art therapist will lead students through activities including making a therapeutic collage and experimenting with watercolor paint and oil pastels. Students will leave this workshop with ideas on how to use art to relieve stress in their daily lives. Art beginners are welcome. This event is sponsored by Art Gives and the Counseling Center.

Express your stress workshop (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/05/express-your-stress-workshop/)
When: Friday, 5-7pm
Where: Ames Hall, Homewood Campus
Summary: Express Your Stress is a free workshop created to give Hopkins students a fun opportunity to relieve stress and learn how to use art to improve their well being. Peggy Kolodny, a professional art therapist will lead students through activities including making a therapeutic collage and experimenting with watercolor paint and oil pastels. Students will leave this workshop with ideas on how to use art to relieve stress in their daily lives. Art beginners welcome. This is sponsored by the Counseling Center.

This year, the theme is "Our Best Selves" and the event supports The Family Tree, a Baltimore organization that helps prevent child abuse while empowering families and building communities.

ChemBE Spring Seminar Series: Rigoberto Hernandez (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/04/chembe-spring-seminar-series-rigoberto-hernandez/)
When: Today, 10:30-11:30am
Where: Krieger Hall, Homewood Campus
Summary: Dr. Rigoberto Hernandez, a professor of Chemistry at Johns Hopkins University, will give a talk entitled "Dynamical Consistency in Sustainable Nanoparticles" for the Department of Chemical and Biomolecular Engineering's ChemBE Seminar Series.

The Randolph Bromery Spring 2019 Seminar Series: Michael Ackerson (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/04/the-randolph-bromery-spring-2019-seminar-series-michael-ackerson/)
When: Today, 12-1pm
Where: Olin Hall, Homewood Campus
Summary: Dr. Michael Ackerson, a geologist at Smithsonian National Museum of Natural History, will give a talk entitled "Partially-molten Granites at 500 °C? Reimagining Crustal Magmatism" for the Department of Earth & Planetary Sciences.

Book signing and panel: "The Farm Bill: A Citizen's Guide" (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/04/the-farm-bill-a-citizens-guide-book-signing-and-panel/)
When: Today, 12-1:15pm
Where: School of Public Health, East Baltimore Campus
Summary: The Farm Bill is the most significant legislation affecting agriculture in the U.S. and generates intense debate when it is revisited every five to seven years. Beyond agriculture, the bill also affects nutrition assistance, habitat conservation, international trade, and more. This panel will help us decipher the Farm Bill and suggest ways to improve it.

Cell Biology Seminar: Dr. Antony Rosen (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/04/cell-biology-seminar-dr-antony-rosen/)
When: Today, 12-1pm
Where: 1830 Building, East Baltimore Campus
Summary: The Cell Biology Department will host Dr. Antony Rosen, vice dean for research and professor of Medicine, Cell Biology, and Pathology at the Johns Hopkins University School of Medicine, who will deliver a talk titled "Autoantibodies in the Rheumatic Diseases: Markers of the Primordial Landmass?"

Neuroscience Research Seminar: Piali Sengupta (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/04/neuroscience-research-seminar-piali-sengupta/)
When: Today, 1-2pm
Where: Preclinical Teaching Building, East Baltimore Campus
Summary: Dr. Piali Sengupta, a professor of Biology at Brandeis University, will give a talk entitled "Feeling the Heat: Thomosensation and Thermosensory Behavioral Plasticity in C. Elegans." The talk is hosted by Dr. Alex Kolodkin, a professor of neuroscience at the Johns Hopkins School of Medicine.

Dept. of Mechanical Engineering Spring Seminar Series: Pablo D. Zavattieri (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/04/department-of-mechanical-engineering-spring-seminar-series-pablo-zavattieri/)
When: Today, 3-4pm
Where: Mudd Hall, Homewood Campus
Summary: Dr. Pablo D. Zavattieri, a professor of Civil Engineering at Purdue University, will give a talk entitled "Uncovering New Mechanisms in Biological and Engineering Architectured Materials" for the Department of Mechanical Engineering.

Cognitive Science Colloquium: Ellen Lau (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/04/cognitive-science-colloquium-ellen-lau/)
When: Today, 3:30-5pm
Where: Krieger Hall, Homewood Campus
Summary: Dr. Ellen Lau, assistant professor of Linguistics at the University of Maryland, will present "Neural Measures of Structured Linguisticrepresentations" for the Department of Cognitive Science.

19th Annual Daniel Nathans Lecture: Dr. Mary-Claire King (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/04/19th-annual-daniel-nathans-lecture-in-the-department-of-molecular-biology-and-genetics/)
When: Today, 4-5pm
Where: Wood Basic Science Building, East Baltimore Campus
Summary: Dr. Mary-Claire King, a professor of Medical Genetics and Genome Sciences at the University of Washington and an American Cancer Society Professor, will present "Genetics of Inherited Breast and Ovarian Cancer: From Gene Discovery to Precision Medicine and Public Health" as the 19th Annual Daniel Nathans Lecture for the Department of Molecular Biology and Genetics.

English T&S Lecture: Robert Bernasconi (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/04/english-ts-lecture-chattel-slavery-as-punishment-stages-in-the-history-of-an-argument-robert-bernasconi-penn-state-university/)
When: Today, 4:15-6:15pm
Where: Gilman Hall, Homewood Campus
Summary: The Johns Hopkins English Department's Tudor and Stuart Lecture Series presents a talk by Robert Bernasconi, a professor of Philosophy and African American Studies at Penn State University, entitled, "Chattel Slavery as Punishment: Stages in the History of an Argument."

Where: Homewood Campus
Summary: The theme of the interdisciplinary 8th Annual Johns Hopkins University Program in Racism, Immigration, and Citizenship Conference is "Eyes on Surveillance: (In)security in Everyday Life." This year's conference interrogates the normalization of surveillance in our everyday life.

When: Friday, 12-1pm
Where: Gilman Hall, Homewood Campus

Division of Health Sciences Informatics Grand Rounds: Dr. Muhammad Abdul-Mageed (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/05/dhsi-grand-rounds-advances-in-deep-representation-learning-and-applications-to-health/)
When: Friday, 12:45-1:45pm
Where: East Baltimore Campus
Summary: Dr. Muhammad Abdul-Mageed, an assistant professor at the University of British Columbia's iSchool, cross appointed with the Department of Linguistics, and an associate member of the Department of Computer Science, will give a talk entitled "Advances in Deep Representation Learning and Applications to Health" as part of the Division of Health Sciences Informatics's Grand Rounds.

The 2019 Gary Laben Lecture featuring Dr. Kathleen Allen (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/05/the-2019-gary-laben-lecture-featuring-dr-kathleen-allen/)
When: Friday, 1:30-2:45pm
Where: Gilman Hall, Homewood Campus

April 3, 2019 Powered by the Hub

Announcements for students on JHU’s Homewood campus

Announcements

Student Employment+Internships

Gap year and year of service opportunities (https://hub.jhu.edu/announcements/2019/04/01/gap-year-year-of-service-opportunities/)
Many gap year programs offering year-long service-based programs use the CSC community bulletin to advertise to graduating students.

Student Organizations+Activities

2020 Student Philanthropy Association application (https://hub.jhu.edu/announcements/2019/04/01/2020-student-philanthropy-association-application/)
The Student Philanthropy Association (SPA) application is now open. The Association is looking for the next crop of outstanding student-leaders to educate their peers on why philanthropy is important and how they can give back to the Hopkins community.

Short story contest open for submissions (https://hub.jhu.edu/announcements/2019/04/01/short-story-contest-open-for-submissions/)
Short fiction contest open to all undergraduates. There is no specific topic or prompt, so be imaginative. The best story will earn its author a $25 Amazon gift card.

Last chance to apply to be a peer health educator (https://hub.jhu.edu/announcements/2019/03/18/last-chance-to-apply-to-be-a-peer-health-educator/)
Gain public health experience as you help to make JHU a healthier place.

Free climbing trip with JHOC (https://hub.jhu.edu/announcements/2019/03/09/free-climbing-trip-with-jhoc-1/)
Come climbing with JHOC at Seneca Rocks on Sunday, April 21st. Registration opens tomorrow, April 4th, on the website at http://outdoors.johnshopkins.edu/trips/.

Free hiking trip with JHOC (https://hub.jhu.edu/announcements/2019/03/09/free-hiking-trip-with-jhoc/)
Come hiking with JHOC at Loch Raven Reservoir on Saturday, April 20th. Registration opens tomorrow, April 4th, on the website at http://outdoors.johnshopkins.edu/trips/.

Free backpacking trip with JHOC (https://hub.jhu.edu/announcements/2019/03/09/free-backpacking-trip-with-jhoc/)
Come backpacking with JHOC on the Appalachian Trail from April 19-20th. Registration opens tomorrow, April 4th, on the website at http://outdoors.johnshopkins.edu/trips/.

Register for Upcoming Events

Spring Fair headliner concert tickets (https://hub.jhu.edu/announcements/2019/04/02/spring-fair-headliner-concert-tickets/)
Announcing the start of Spring Fair headliner concert ticket sales.

Participate in the premiere sustainability hackathon at Johns Hopkins University on April 20th, 2019. GreenHacks aims to bring together students from diverse areas of expertise across all Hopkins-affiliated campuses to develop innovative solutions.

1st Annual Diversity & Inclusion Poster Session

Upcoming Events

Arts+Culture

Movements: Black Print Culture in the United States, 1773–1940 (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/02/11/black-print-culture/)
When: Feb 11 - May 24, 12am
Where: MSE Library, Homewood Campus
Summary: An exhibition exploring the circulation and contribution of black print culture through original items drawn from the Sheridan Libraries Special Collections.

The Rosenburg—The Federal Ministry of Justice in the Shadow of the Nazi Past (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/03/28/the-rosenburgthe-federal-ministry-of-justice-in-the-shadow-of-the-nazi-past/)
When: March 28 - May 1, 12am
Where: MSE Library, Homewood Campus
Summary: This traveling multimedia exhibition by the German Federal Ministry of Justice and Consumer Protection explores the Nazi infiltration of the post-1945 West German justice ministry and the legal and political consequences for the young Federal Republic.

Artist Sandy Rodríguez presents the Codex Rodríguez-Mondragón (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/03/artist-sandy-rodrguez-presents-the-codex-rodrguez-mondragn/)
When: Today, 3-4:15pm
Where: Gilman Hall, Homewood Campus
Summary: Join Los Angeles-based Chicana artist Sandy Rodriguez for a talk about her latest series, Codez Rodriguez-Mondragón, which draws on pre-contact and post-conquest Mesoamerican codez practices to tell a contemporary Chicana story of the Americas.

Computer Music Seminar: Andrea Pejrolo (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/03/peabody-computer-music-seminar-andrea-pejrolo/)
When: Today, 6-7:30pm
Where: Centre Street Performance Studio, Peabody Institute

When: Today, 7:30-9:30pm
Summary: Edward Polochick, conductor

Where: Hilda and Douglas Goodwin Recital Hall, Peabody Institute

When: Thursday, 2:30-4:30pm

Where: Campus: Homewood Campus, Building: Center For Social Concern
Summary: Come Learn about the new France-Merrick Civic Fellowship. This opportunity is open to rising juniors and seniors with an interest in a social and civic issue or community of focus.

Teach For America happy hour (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/03/teach-for-america-appy-hour/)
When: Today, 7-9pm
Where: MSE Library, Homewood Campus
Summary: Students who want to create systemic change in society, are interested in making immediate impact, and/or want to learn how to stand out and be a better leader should drop by the MSE Library M-level (near the Brody entrance) and learn more about Teach For America's final junior deadline on April 12th. There, they will learn what they need to send in a great application, and also learn more about early engagement opportunities like internships, conferences, and more.

10th Annual Conference in Public Health (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/04/10th-annual-conference-in-public-health/)
When: Thursday, 3-8pm
Where: Gilman Hall, Homewood Campus
Summary: The Johns Hopkins Public Health Student Forum is hosting the 10th Annual Undergraduate Conference in Public Health with a keynote speech by Dr. Rebecca Martin, director of the CDC's Center for Global Health.

Book signing and panel: "The Farm Bill: A Citizen's Guide" (https://hub.jhu.edu/events/2019/04/04/the-farm-bill-a-citizens-guide-book-signing-and-panel/)
When: Thursday, 12-1:15pm
Where: School of Public Health, East Baltimore Campus
Summary: The Farm Bill is the most significant legislation affecting agriculture in the U.S. and generates intense debate when it is revisited every five to seven years. Beyond agriculture, the bill also affects nutrition assistance, habitat conservation, international trade, and more. This panel will help us decipher the Farm Bill and suggest ways to improve it.
